## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Controller Runtime Reconciler Registration

## Your Task

Trace how a controller registers itself with the controller-runtime Manager in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files that define the Reconciler interface, implement SetupWithManager, and wire the controller into the manager's reconcile loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

Here's the complete picture:

## The Kubernetes Internal Controller Manager Framework

### 1. The "Reconciler" Interface Equivalent

The kubernetes codebase has two relevant interfaces:

**`controller.Interface`** (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go):
```go
type Interface interface {
    Name() string
}
```
This is the base interface for controllers. It's analogous to `reconcile.Reconciler` in controller-runtime.

**`InitFunc`** (cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go):
```go
type InitFunc func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller controller.Interface, enabled bool, err error)
```
This is the function type that initializes a controller. It's analogous to `SetupWithManager` in controller-runtime.

### 2. The "SetupWithManager" Equivalent

Each controller has a `newXxxControllerDescriptor()` function that creates a `ControllerDescriptor` with the controller's name and init function. This is analogous to `SetupWithManager` in controller-runtime.

For example, in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/core.go`:

662026-03-08T20:29:47.391284agentmessage-
The `/workspace/answer.json` has been written. Here is a complete summary of all findings:

---

## How a Controller Registers with the "Manager" in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32.0

### Critical Finding: No controller-runtime

`sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime` is **completely absent** from `kubernetes/kubernetes`. The vendor directory under `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/` contains only `json`, `yaml`, `kustomize`, `structured-merge-diff`, `knftables`, and `apiserver-network-proxy`. The only occurrence of the string `"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime"` in the entire repo is a comment in a test file. There is no `Reconciler` interface, no `SetupWithManager`, and no `ctrl.Manager` from that library.

Instead, the codebase uses its own internal controller manager framework (`k8s.io/controller-manager`). Here is the complete trace:

---

### 1. The "Reconciler Interface" Equivalent

**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`

```go
type Interface interface {
    Name() string
}
```

This is the base interface every controller must satisfy. Two optional extensions exist:
- `controller.Debuggable` → `DebuggingHandler() http.Handler` (mounts `/debug/controllers/<name>/`)
- `controller.HealthCheckable` → `HealthChecker() healthz.UnnamedHealthChecker` (exposes `/healthz` check)

---

### 2. The "SetupWithManager" Equivalent — `InitFunc` + `ControllerDescriptor`

**File:** `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`

```go
// InitFunc is the "SetupWithManager" equivalent
type InitFunc func(ctx context.Context, controllerContext ControllerContext, controllerName string) (controller controller.Interface, enabled bool, err error)

// ControllerDescriptor binds a name to its InitFunc
type ControllerDescriptor struct {
    name                      string
  
... (truncated)

  "thought": "Now I have a comprehensive picture of the kubernetes/kubernetes codebase. The task is asking about the internal pattern that is analogous to controller-runtime.\n\nHere's the complete picture:\n\n## The Kubernetes Internal Controller Manager Framework\n\n### 1. The \"Reconciler\" Interface Equivalent\n\nThe kubernetes codebase has two relevant interfaces:\n\n**`controller.Interface`** (staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go):\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Name() string\n}\n```\nThis is the base interface for controllers. The \"SetupWithManager\" Equivalent\n\nEach controller has a `newXxxControllerDescriptor()` function that creates a `ControllerDescriptor` with the controller's name and init function.   "thought": "Now I have a comprehensive picture. Let me also look at the `pkg/controller/servicecidrs` directory to see the controller implementation.\n\nActually, I have enough information. Let me now write the answer.json file.\n\nThe key findings are:\n\n1. **kubernetes/kubernetes does NOT use sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime**. The vendor directory does not contain controller-runtime. The only reference to \"sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime\" is in a test comment.\n\n2. **The kubernetes codebase has its own internal controller manager framework** that is analogous to controller-runtime. The key components are:\n\n   a. **`controller.Interface`** - defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go` - This is the base interface for controllers (analogous to `reconcile.Reconciler` in controller-runtime). It requires only a `Name() string` method.\n\n   b. **`InitFunc`** - defined in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` - This is the function type that initializes a controller. It's analogous to `SetupWithManager` in controller-runtime.\n\n   c. **`ControllerDescriptor`** - defined in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` - This wraps a controller's name and init function.\n\n   d. **`ControllerContext`** - defined in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` - This is the \"Manager\" equivalent, providing clients, informers, and other shared resources.\n\n   e. **`NewControllerDescriptors()`** - defined in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` - This registers all controllers.\n\n   f. **`StartControllers()`** and **`StartController()`** - defined in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` - These start all controllers.\n\n3. **The registration pattern** is:\n   - Each controller has a `newXxxControllerDescriptor()` function that creates a `ControllerDescriptor` with the controller's name and init function.\n   - The `ControllerDescriptor` is registered in `NewControllerDescriptors()`.\n   - When the controller manager starts, `StartControllers()` is called, which calls `StartController()` for each controller.\n   - `StartController()` calls the controller's `initFunc`, which creates the controller and starts its reconcile loop (typically via `go controller.Run(ctx)`).\n\n4. **The reconcile loop** is implemented by each controller individually, typically using a `workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface` and a `Run()` method that starts worker goroutines.\n\n5. **The generic controller pattern** (for admission policy controllers) in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/policy/internal/generic` has a more controller-runtime-like pattern with a `Controller[T]` interface and a `reconciler` function.\n\nNow let me write the answer.json file.\n"
